           <dt>iti 2</dt>
           <dd><em>iti</em> ind. (fr. pronominal base 3. <em>i</em>), in this manner, thus (in its original signification <em>iti</em> refers to something that has been said or thought, or lays stress on what precedes </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; in the Br&#x0101;hma&#x1e47;as it is often equivalent to 'as you know', reminding the hearer or reader of certain customs, conditions, &amp;c. supposed to be known to him). In quotations of every kind <em>iti</em> means that the preceding words are the very words which some person has or might have spoken, and placed thus at the end of a speech it serves the purpose of inverted commas (<em>ity uktv&#x0101;</em>, having so said </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>iti k&#x1e5b;tv&#x0101;</em>, having so considered, having so decided). It may often have reference merely to what is passing in the mind, e.g. <em>b&#x0101;lo'pi n&#x00e2;vamantavyo manu&#x1e63;ya iti bh&#x016b;mipa&#x1e25;</em>, a king, though a child, is not to be despised, saying to one's self, 'he is a mortal', (Gr. 928.) In dram. <em>iti tath&#x0101; karoti</em> means 'after these words he acts thus.' Sometimes <em>iti</em> is used to include under one head a number of separate objects aggregated together (e.g. <em>ijy&#x00e2;dhyayanad&#x0101;n&#x0101;ni tapa&#x1e25; satya&#x1e43; k&#x1e63;am&#x0101; dama&#x1e25;</em> <em>alobha iti m&#x0101;rgo'yam</em>, 'sacrificing, studying, liberality, penance, truth, patience, self-restraint, absence of desire', this course of conduct, &amp;c.) <em>iti</em> is sometimes followed by <em>evam</em>, <em>iva</em>, or a demonstrative pronoun pleonastically (e.g. <em>t&#x0101;m br&#x016b;y&#x0101;d bhavat&#x012b;7ty evam</em>, her he may call 'lady', thus). <em>iti</em> may form an adverbial compound with the name of an author (e.g. <em>iti-p&#x0101;&#x1e47;ini</em>, thus according to P&#x0101;&#x1e47;ini). It may also express the act of calling attention (lo! behold!) It may have some other significations, e.g. something additional (as in <em>ity&#x0101;di</em>, et caetera), order, arrangement specific or distinctive, and identity. It is used by native commentators after quoting a rule to express 'according to such a rule' (e.g. <em>anud&#x0101;tta&#x1e45;ita ity &#x0101;tmanepadam bhavati</em>, according to the rule of P&#x0101;&#x1e47;ini i, 3, 12, the &#x0100;tmane-pada takes place). <em>kim iti</em> = <em>kim</em>, wherefore, why? (In the &#x015a;atapatha-br&#x0101;hma&#x1e47;a <em>ti</em> occurs for <em>iti</em> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Pr&#x0101;k&#x1e5b;it">Pr&#x0101;k&#x1e5b;it.</a> <em>ti</em> and <em>tti</em>.)</dd>

           <dt>&#x22d9; itikatha </dt>
           <dd><em>&#x25cb;katha</em> mfn. unworthy of trust, not fit to be credited </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; wicked, lost </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; (<em>&#x0101;</em>), f. unmeaning or nonsensical discourse </dd>

           <dt>&#x22d9; itikara&#x1e47;iya </dt>
           <dd><em>&#x25cb;kara&#x1e47;iya</em> [<a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Kir">Kir.</a> vii, 17] or mfn. proper or necessary to be done according to certain conditions</dd>

           <dt>&#x22d9; itikartavya </dt>
           <dd><em>&#x25cb;kartavya</em> or mfn. proper or necessary to be done according to certain conditions</dd>

           <dt>&#x22d9; itik&#x0101;rya </dt>
           <dd><em>&#x25cb;k&#x0101;rya</em> or mfn. proper or necessary to be done according to certain conditions</dd>

           <dt>itth&#x0101; </dt>
           <dd><em>itth&#x0101;&#x0341;</em> ind. Ved. thus </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; (often used in the &#x1e5a;ig-veda, and sometimes only to lay stress on a following word </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; therefore by native etymologists [<a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Nir">Nir.</a>] considered as a particle of affirmation.) <em>itth&#x0101;</em> is often connected with words expressing devotion to the gods &amp;c. in the sense of thus, truly, really </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; especially with <em>dh&#x012b;</em> as an adjective. Hence <em>itth&#x0101;-dh&#x012b;</em> = such, i.e. true (<em>saty&#x0101;</em>) or real worship. Similarly, <em>itth&#x0101;-dh&#x012b;&#x0341;</em> mfn. so devout, so pious, i.e. very devout </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; performing such or true works {cf. S&#x0101;y.} <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#AV">AV.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Ka&#x1e6d;hUp">Ka&#x1e6d;hUp.</a></dd>

           <dt>itth&#x0101;t </dt>

           <dt>itya </dt>
           <dd><em>itya</em> &amp;c., <em>itvan</em>, &amp;c. See p. 163, col. 3</dd>

           <dt>id </dt>
           <dd><em>&#x00ed;d</em> ind. Ved. (probably the neut. form of the pronom. base <em>i</em>, See 3. <em>i</em> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; a particle of affirmation) even, just, only </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; indeed, assuredly (especially, in strengthening an antithesis, e.g. <em>y&#x00e1;th&#x0101; v&#x00e1;&#x015b;anti dev&#x0101;&#x0341;s t&#x00e1;h&#x00ea;&#x0341;d asat</em>, as the gods wish it, thus indeed it will be <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> viii, 28, 4 </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>d&#x00ed;psanta &#x00ed;d rip&#x00e1;vo n&#x00e2;&#x0341;ha debhu&#x1e25;</em>, the enemies wishing indeed to hurt were in nowise able to hurt <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> i, 147, 3). <em>id</em> is often added to words expressing excess or exclusion (e.g. <em>vi&#x015b;va it</em>, every one indeed </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>&#x015b;a&#x015b;vad it</em>, constantly indeed </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>eka it</em>, one only). At the beginning of sentences it often adds emphasis to pronouns, prepositions, particles (e.g. <em>tvam it</em>, thou indeed </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>yadi it</em>, if indeed, &amp;c.) <em>id</em> occurs often in the &#x1e5a;ig-veda and Atharva-veda, seldom in the Br&#x0101;hma&#x1e47;as, and its place is taken in classical Sansk&#x1e5b;it by <em>eva</em> and other particles</dd>

           <dt>idam 1</dt>
           <dd><em>id&#x00e1;m</em> <em>ay&#x00e1;m</em>, <em>iy&#x00e1;m</em>, <em>id&#x00e1;m</em> (fr. <em>id</em> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#U&#x1e47;">U&#x1e47;.</a> iv, 156 </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; g. <em>sarv&#x00e2;di</em> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#P&#x0101;&#x1e47;">P&#x0101;&#x1e47;.</a> 1-1, 27 <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Vop">Vop.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; a kind of neut. of the pronom. base 3. <em>i</em> with <em>am</em> [<a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Lat">Lat.</a> <em>is</em>, <em>ea</em>, <em>id</em>, and <em>idem</em>] </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; the regular forms are partly derived from the pronom. base <em>a</em> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; See Gr. 224 </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; the Veda exhibits various irregular formations, e.g. fr. pronom. base <em>a</em>, an inst. <em>en&#x0101;&#x0341;</em>, <em>ay&#x0101;&#x0341;</em> <em>used in general adverbially</em>, and gen. loc. du. <em>ay&#x00f3;s</em>, and perhaps also <em>av&#x00f3;s</em>, in <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> vi, 67, 11 ; vii, 67, 4 ; x, 132, 5 [<a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#BRD">BRD.</a>] </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; fr. the base <em>ima</em>, a gen. sing. <em>im&#x00e1;sya</em>, only <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; the <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> has in a few instances the irregular accentuation <em>&#x00e1;smai</em>, v, 39, 5, &amp;c </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>&#x00e1;sya</em>, iv, 15, 5, &amp;c </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>&#x0101;&#x0341;bhis</em>, vi, 25, 2, &amp;c.: the forms derived fr. <em>a</em> are used enclitically if they take the place of the third personal pronoun, do not stand at the beginning of a verse or period, and have no peculiar stress laid upon them), this, this here, referring to something near the speaker </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; known, present </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; (opposed to <em>adas</em> e.g. <em>aya&#x1e43; loka&#x1e25;</em> or <em>ida&#x1e43; vi&#x015b;vam</em> or <em>ida&#x1e43; sarvam</em>, this earthly world, this universe </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>ayam agni&#x1e25;</em>, this fire which burns on the earth </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; but <em>as&#x0101;v agni&#x1e25;</em>, that fire in the sky, i. e. the lightning: so also <em>idam</em> or <em>iyam</em> alone sometimes signifies 'this earth' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>ime sma&#x1e25;</em>, here we are.) <em>idam</em> often refers to something immediately following, whereas <em>etad</em> points to what precedes (e.g. <em>&#x015b;rutv&#x00e2;itad idam &#x016b;cu&#x1e25;</em>, having heard that they said this). <em>idam</em> occurs connected with <em>yad</em>, <em>tad</em>, <em>etad</em>, <em>kim</em>, and a personal pronoun, partly to point out anything more distinctly and emphatically, partly pleonastically (e.g. <em>tad ida&#x1e43; v&#x0101;kyam</em>, this speech here following <font color="#FF0000" font size=-2><a name="p165-3"></a>[Page 165, Column 3]</font> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>so'ya&#x1e43; vid&#x016b;&#x1e63;aka&#x1e25;</em>, this Vid&#x016b;shaka here)</dd>

           <dt>&#x226b; idadvasu </dt>
           <dd><em>id&#x00e1;d-vasu</em> mfn. rich in this and that <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#AV">AV.</a> xiii, 4, 54</dd>

           <dt>&#x22d9; id&#x0101;vatsara </dt>

           <dd>&#x2022; one of the five years in which gifts of clothes and food are productive of great rewards         <br>          <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#AV">AV.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#VS">VS.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#MaitrS">MaitrS.</a> &amp;c.            <dt>&#x226b; id&#x0101;ni </dt>

           <dt>&#x226b; id&#x0101;n&#x012b;m </dt>
           <dd><em>i-d&#x0101;&#x0341;n&#x012b;m</em> ind. now, at this moment, in this case, just, even (with gen. of <em>ahan</em> e.g. <em>id&#x0101;n&#x012b;m ahna&#x1e25;</em>, this present day, 'now-a-days' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>id&#x0101;n&#x012b;m eva</em>, just now </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; immediately </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>id&#x0101;n&#x012b;m api</em>, in this case too </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>tata id&#x0101;n&#x012b;m</em>, thereupon, then) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#&#x015a;Br">&#x015a;Br.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Ait">Ait.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Ragh">Ragh.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; (in rare cases it is an expletive, affecting but slightly the sense)</dd>

           <dd><em>ind&#x016b;ra</em> m. a rat, a mouse [cf. <em>undura</em>, <em>unduru</em>] <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#L">L.</a></dd>

           <dt>indra </dt>
           <dd><em>&#x00ed;ndra</em> m. (for etym. as given by native authorities <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Nir">Nir.</a> x, 8 <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#S&#x0101;y">S&#x0101;y.</a> on <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> i, 3, 4 <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#U&#x1e47;">U&#x1e47;.</a> ii, 28 </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; according to <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#BRD">BRD.</a> fr. <em>in</em> = &#x221a;<em>inv</em> with suff. <em>ra</em> preceded by inserted <em>d</em>, meaning 'to subdue, conquer' <font color="#FF0000" font size=-2><a name="p166-2"></a>[Page 166, Column 2]</font> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; according to Muir, S. <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#T">T.</a> v, 119, for <em>sindra</em> fr. &#x221a;<em>syand</em>, 'to drop' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; more probably from &#x221a;<em>ind</em>, 'to drop', q.v., and connected with <em>indu</em> above), the god of the atmosphere and sky </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; the Indian Jupiter Pluvius or lord of rain (who in Vedic mythology reigns over the deities of the intermediate region or atmosphere </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; he fights against and conquers with his thunder-bolt [<em>vajra</em>] the demons of darkness, and is in general a symbol of generous heroism </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>indra</em> was not originally lord of the gods of the sky, but his deeds were most useful to mankind, and he was therefore addressed in prayers and hymns more than any other deity, and ultimately superseded the more lofty and spiritual Varu&#x1e47;a </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; in the later mythology <em>indra</em> is subordinated to the triad Brahman, Vish&#x1e47;u, and &#x015a;iva, but remained the chief of all other deities in the popular mind)         <br>          <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#AV">AV.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#&#x015a;Br">&#x015a;Br.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Mn">Mn.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#MBh">MBh.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#R">R.</a> &amp;c. &amp;c </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; (he is also regent of the east quarter, and considered one of the twelve &#x0100;dityas) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Mn">Mn.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#R">R.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Su&#x015b;r">Su&#x015b;r.</a> &amp;c </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; in the Ved&#x0101;nta he is identified with the supreme being </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; a prince </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; ifc. best, excellent, the first, the chief (of any class of objects </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; cf. <em>sur&#x00ea;ndra</em>, <em>r&#x0101;j&#x00ea;ndra</em>, <em>parvat&#x00ea;ndra</em>, &amp;c.) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Mn">Mn.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Hit">Hit.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; the pupil of the right eye (that of the left being called Indr&#x0101;&#x1e47;&#x012b; or Indra's wife) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#&#x015a;Br">&#x015a;Br.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#B&#x1e5b;&#x0100;rUp">B&#x1e5b;&#x0100;rUp.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; the number fourteen, S&#x016b;ryas </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; N. of a grammarian </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; of a physician </dd>

           <dt>&#x226b; indriya </dt>
           <dd><em>indriy&#x00e1;</em> mfn. fit for or belonging to or agreeable to Indra <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#AV">AV.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#VS">VS.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; m. a companion of Indra(?) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> i, 107, 2 <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#AV">AV.</a> xix, 27, 1 </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; (<em>am</em>), n. power, force, the quality which belongs especially to the mighty Indra         <br>          <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#AV">AV.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#VS">VS.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#TS">TS.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#AitBr">AitBr.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#&#x015a;Br">&#x015a;Br.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; exhibition of power, powerful act <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#VS">VS.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; bodily power, power of the senses </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; virile power <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#AV">AV.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#VS">VS.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#&#x015a;Br">&#x015a;Br.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; semen virile <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#VS">VS.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#K&#x0101;ty&#x015a;r">K&#x0101;ty&#x015a;r.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#MBh">MBh.</a> &amp;c </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; faculty of sense, sense, organ of sense <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#AV">AV.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Su&#x015b;r">Su&#x015b;r.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Mn">Mn.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Ragh">Ragh.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Kir">Kir.</a> &amp;c </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; the number five as symbolical of the five senses. (In addition to the five organs of perception, <em>buddh&#x012b;7ndriy&#x0101;&#x1e47;i</em> or <em>j&#x00f1;&#x0101;n&#x00ea;ndriy&#x0101;&#x1e47;i</em>, i.e. eye, ear, nose, tongue, and skin, the Hind&#x016b;s enumerate five organs of action, <em>karm&#x00ea;ndriy&#x0101;&#x1e47;i</em> i.e. larynx, hand, foot, anus, and parts of generation </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; between these ten organs and the soul or <em>&#x0101;tman</em> stands <em>manas</em> or mind, considered as an eleventh organ </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; in the Ved&#x0101;nta, <em>manas</em>, <em>buddhi</em>, <em>aha&#x1e43;k&#x0101;ra</em>, and <em>citta</em> form the four inner or internal organs, <em>antar-indriy&#x0101;&#x1e47;i</em>, so that according to this reckoning the organs are fourteen in number, each being presided over by its own ruler or <em>niyant&#x1e5b;</em> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; thus, the eye by the Sun, the ear by the Quarters of the world, the nose by the two A&#x015b;vins, the tongue by Pracetas, the skin by the Wind, the voice by Fire, the hand by Indra, the foot by Vish&#x1e47;u, the anus by Mitra, the parts of generation by Praj&#x0101;pati, manas by the Moon, buddhi by Brahman, aha&#x1e43;k&#x0101;ra by &#x015a;iva, citta by Vishnu as Acyuta </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; in the Ny&#x0101;ya philosophy each organ is connected with its own peculiar element, the nose with the Earth, the tongue with Water, the eye with Light or Fire, the skin with Air, the ear with Ether </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; the Jainas divide the whole creation into five sections, according to the number of organs attributed to each being.)</dd>

           <dt>&#x22d9; indriyak&#x0101;ma </dt>

           <dt>iva </dt>
           <dd><em>iva</em> ind. (fr. pronominal base 3. <em>i</em>), like, in the same manner as (in this sense = <em>yath&#x0101;</em>, and used correlatively to <em>tath&#x0101;</em>) </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; as it were, as if (e.g. <em>path&#x00ea;va</em>, as if on a path) </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; in a certain manner, in some measure, a little, perhaps (in qualification or mitigation of a strong assertion) </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; nearly, almost, about (e.g. <em>muh&#x016b;rtam iva</em>, almost an hour) </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; so, just so, just, exactly, indeed, very (especially after words which involve some restriction, e.g. <em>&#x012b;&#x1e63;ad iva</em>, just a little </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>ki&#x1e43;cid iva</em>, just a little bit: and after a negation, e.g. <em>na cir&#x0101;d iva</em>, very soon). <em>iva</em> is connected vaguely, and somewhat pleonastically, with an interrogative pronoun or adverb (e.g. <em>kim iva</em>, what? <em>katham iva</em>, how could that possibly be? <em>kv&#x00ea;va</em>, where, I should like to know?). In the Pada texts of the &#x1e5a;ig, Yajur, and Atharva-veda, and by native grammarians, <em>iva</em> is considered to be enclitic, and therefore compounded with the word after which it stands <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#AV">AV.</a> &amp;c. &amp;c</dd>

           <dt>&#x22d9; ivopam&#x0101; </dt>
           <dd><em>iv&#x00f4;pam&#x0101;</em> f. a kind of simile (in which <em>iva</em> is employed) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Bha&#x1e6d;&#x1e6d;">Bha&#x1e6d;&#x1e6d;.</a> x, 30</dd>
